    1841             : // See if a special block-size reflow needs to occur and if so,

    1886           1 : }
    1887             : 
    1888             : /******************************************************************************************
    1889             :  * Before reflow, intrinsic inline-size calculation is done using GetMinISize
    1890             :  * and GetPrefISize.  This used to be known as pass 1 reflow.
    1891             :  *
    1892             :  * After the intrinsic isize calculation, the table determines the
    1893             :  * column widths using BalanceColumnISizes() and
    1894             :  * then reflows each child again with a constrained avail isize. This reflow is referred to
    1895             :  * as the pass 2 reflow.
    1896             :  *
    1897             :  * A special bsize reflow (pass 3 reflow) can occur during an initial or resize reflow
    1898             :  * if (a) a row group, row, cell, or a frame inside a cell has a percent bsize but no computed
    1899             :  * bsize or (b) in paginated mode, a table has a bsize. (a) supports percent nested tables
    1900             :  * contained inside cells whose bsizes aren't known until after the pass 2 reflow. (b) is
    1901             :  * necessary because the table cannot split until after the pass 2 reflow. The mechanics of
    1902             :  * the special bsize reflow (variety a) are as follows:
    1903             :  *
    1904             :  * 1) Each table related frame (table, row group, row, cell) implements NeedsSpecialReflow()
    1905             :  *    to indicate that it should get the reflow. It does this when it has a percent bsize but
    1906             :  *    no computed bsize by calling CheckRequestSpecialBSizeReflow(). This method calls
    1907             :  *    RequestSpecialBSizeReflow() which calls SetNeedSpecialReflow() on its ancestors until
    1908             :  *    it reaches the containing table and calls SetNeedToInitiateSpecialReflow() on it. For
    1909             :  *    percent bsize frames inside cells, during DidReflow(), the cell's NotifyPercentBSize()
    1910             :  *    is called (the cell is the reflow state's mPercentBSizeObserver in this case).
    1911             :  *    NotifyPercentBSize() calls RequestSpecialBSizeReflow().
    1912             :  *
    1913             :  * XXX (jfkthame) This comment appears to be out of date; it refers to methods/flags
    1914             :  *                that are no longer present in the code.
    1915             :  * 2) After the pass 2 reflow, if the table's NeedToInitiateSpecialReflow(true) was called, it
    1916             :  *    will do the special bsize reflow, setting the reflow state's mFlags.mSpecialBSizeReflow
    1917             :  *    to true and mSpecialHeightInitiator to itself. It won't do this if IsPrematureSpecialHeightReflow()
    1918             :  *    returns true because in that case another special bsize reflow will be coming along with the
    1919             :  *    containing table as the mSpecialHeightInitiator. It is only relevant to do the reflow when
    1920             :  *    the mSpecialHeightInitiator is the containing table, because if it is a remote ancestor, then
    1921             :  *    appropriate bsizes will not be known.
    1922             :  *
    1923             :  * 3) Since the bsizes of the table, row groups, rows, and cells was determined during the pass 2
    1924             :  *    reflow, they return their last desired sizes during the special bsize reflow. The reflow only
    1925             :  *    permits percent bsize frames inside the cells to resize based on the cells bsize and that bsize
    1926             :  *    was determined during the pass 2 reflow.
    1927             :  *
    1928             :  * So, in the case of deeply nested tables, all of the tables that were told to initiate a special
    1929             :  * reflow will do so, but if a table is already in a special reflow, it won't inititate the reflow
    1930             :  * until the current initiator is its containing table. Since these reflows are only received by
    1931             :  * frames that need them and they don't cause any rebalancing of tables, the extra overhead is minimal.
    1932             :  *
    1933             :  * The type of special reflow that occurs during printing (variety b) follows the same mechanism except
    1934             :  * that all frames will receive the reflow even if they don't really need them.
    1935             :  *
    1936             :  * Open issues with the special bsize reflow:
    1937             :  *
    1938             :  * 1) At some point there should be 2 kinds of special bsize reflows because (a) and (b) above are
    1939             :  *    really quite different. This would avoid unnecessary reflows during printing.
    1940             :  * 2) When a cell contains frames whose percent bsizes > 100%, there is data loss (see bug 115245).
    1941             :  *    However, this can also occur if a cell has a fixed bsize and there is no special bsize reflow.
    1942             :  *
    1943             :  * XXXldb Special bsize reflow should really be its own method, not
    1944             :  * part of nsIFrame::Reflow.  It should then call nsIFrame::Reflow on
    1945             :  * the contents of the cells to do the necessary block-axis resizing.

    4220             :  * Collapsing Borders
    4221             :  *
    4222             :  *  The CSS spec says to resolve border conflicts in this order:
    4223             :  *  1) any border with the style HIDDEN wins
    4224             :  *  2) the widest border with a style that is not NONE wins
    4225             :  *  3) the border styles are ranked in this order, highest to lowest precedence:
    4226             :  *     double, solid, dashed, dotted, ridge, outset, groove, inset
    4227             :  *  4) borders that are of equal width and style (differ only in color) have this precedence:
    4228             :  *     cell, row, rowgroup, col, colgroup, table
    4229             :  *  5) if all border styles are NONE, then that's the computed border style.

    4303             : /* BCCellBorder represents a border segment which can be either an inline-dir
    4304             :  * or a block-dir segment. For each segment we need to know the color, width,
    4305             :  * style, who owns it and how long it is in cellmap coordinates.
    4306             :  * Ownership of these segments is important to calculate which corners should
    4307             :  * be bevelled. This structure has dual use, its used first to compute the
    4308             :  * dominant border for inline-dir and block-dir segments and to store the
    4309             :  * preliminary computed border results in the BCCellBorders structure.
    4310             :  * This temporary storage is not symmetric with respect to inline-dir and
    4311             :  * block-dir border segments, its always column oriented. For each column in
    4312             :  * the cellmap there is a temporary stored block-dir and inline-dir segment.
    4313             :  * XXX_Bernd this asymmetry is the root of those rowspan bc border errors
    4314             :  */
    4315             : struct BCCellBorder
    4316             : {
    4317           1 :   BCCellBorder() { Reset(0, 1); }
    4318             :   void Reset(uint32_t aRowIndex, uint32_t aRowSpan);
    4319             :   nscolor       color;    // border segment color
    4320             :   BCPixelSize   width;    // border segment width in pixel coordinates !!
    4321             :   uint8_t       style;    // border segment style, possible values are defined
    4322             :                           // in nsStyleConsts.h as NS_STYLE_BORDER_STYLE_*
    4323             :   BCBorderOwner owner;    // border segment owner, possible values are defined
    4324             :                           // in celldata.h. In the cellmap for each border
    4325             :                           // segment we store the owner and later when
    4326             :                           // painting we know the owner and can retrieve the
    4327             :                           // style info from the corresponding frame
    4328             :   int32_t       rowIndex; // rowIndex of temporary stored inline-dir border
    4329             :                           // segments relative to the table
    4330             :   int32_t       rowSpan;  // row span of temporary stored inline-dir border

    5847             : 
    5848             : /* XXX This comment is still written in physical (horizontal-tb) terms.
    5849             : 
    5850             :    Here is the order for storing border edges in the cell map as a cell is processed. There are
    5851             :    n=colspan top and bottom border edges per cell and n=rowspan left and right border edges per cell.
    5852             : 
    5853             :    1) On the top edge of the table, store the top edge. Never store the top edge otherwise, since
    5854             :       a bottom edge from a cell above will take care of it.
    5855             :    2) On the left edge of the table, store the left edge. Never store the left edge othewise, since
    5856             :       a right edge from a cell to the left will take care of it.
    5857             :    3) Store the right edge (or edges if a row span)
    5858             :    4) Store the bottom edge (or edges if a col span)
    5859             : 
    5860             :    Since corners are computed with only an array of BCCornerInfo indexed by the number-of-cols, corner
    5861             :    calculations are somewhat complicated. Using an array with number-of-rows * number-of-col entries
    5862             :    would simplify this, but at an extra in memory cost of nearly 12 bytes per cell map entry. Collapsing
    5863             :    borders already have about an extra 8 byte per cell map entry overhead (this could be
    5864             :    reduced to 4 bytes if we are willing to not store border widths in nsTableCellFrame), Here are the
    5865             :    rules in priority order for storing cornes in the cell map as a cell is processed. top-left means the
    5866             :    left endpoint of the border edge on the top of the cell. There are n=colspan top and bottom border
    5867             :    edges per cell and n=rowspan left and right border edges per cell.
    5868             : 
    5869             :    1) On the top edge of the table, store the top-left corner, unless on the left edge of the table.
    5870             :       Never store the top-right corner, since it will get stored as a right-top corner.
    5871             :    2) On the left edge of the table, store the left-top corner. Never store the left-bottom corner,
    5872             :       since it will get stored as a bottom-left corner.
    5873             :    3) Store the right-top corner if (a) it is the top right corner of the table or (b) it is not on
    5874             :       the top edge of the table. Never store the right-bottom corner since it will get stored as a
    5875             :       bottom-right corner.
    5876             :    4) Store the bottom-right corner, if it is the bottom right corner of the table. Never store it
    5877             :       otherwise, since it will get stored as either a right-top corner by a cell below or
    5878             :       a bottom-left corner from a cell to the right.
    5879             :    5) Store the bottom-left corner, if (a) on the bottom edge of the table or (b) if the left edge hits
    5880             :       the top side of a colspan in its interior. Never store the corner otherwise, since it will
    5881             :       get stored as a right-top corner by a cell from below.
    5882             : 
    5883             :    XXX the BC-RTL hack - The correct fix would be a rewrite as described in bug 203686.
    5884             :    In order to draw borders in rtl conditions somehow correct, the existing structure which relies
    5885             :    heavily on the assumption that the next cell sibling will be on the right side, has been modified.
    5886             :    We flip the border during painting and during style lookup. Look for tableIsLTR for places where
    5887             :    the flipping is done.
    5888             :  */
    5889             :
